# Java Annotation Processing for Kafka Config Keys

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that use the @ConfigKey and @ConfigDef annotation pattern for configuration documentation: the annotation definitions, the config documentation generator, and the AbstractConfig subclasses that use annotated config keys.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)


Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the Apache Kafka repository and created the `answer.json` file with comprehensive findings.

## Summary of Findings

**Important Discovery:** Apache Kafka uses a **class-based configuration pattern** rather than Java annotations named @ConfigKey and @ConfigDef. The task description refers to annotations that don't actually exist in the codebase.

### What I Found:

**1. Core Configuration Pattern Implementation (2 files):**
- **ConfigDef.java**: Main class for specifying configurations with metadata
- **AbstractConfig.java**: Base class for all configuration classes
- **ConfigKey**: Inner class within ConfigDef for representing individual config keys

**2. Configuration Documentation Generators (2 files):**
- **PredicateDoc.java**: Generates HTML documentation for Kafka Connect predicates
- **TransformationDoc.java**: Generates HTML documentation for Kafka Connect transformations

**3. AbstractConfig Subclasses (53+ files):**
These implement the configuration pattern across different Kafka modules:
- **Client configs**: AdminClientConfig, ConsumerConfig, ProducerConfig
- **Kafka Connect configs**: ConnectorConfig, TaskConfig, WorkerConfig, plus various transform and predicate classes
- **Server configs**: ServerConfigs, KRaftConfigs, ReplicationConfigs, etc.
- **Component configs**: GroupCoordinatorConfig, LogConfig, StreamsConfig, and many others

The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains:
- **files**: 56 relevant Java source files
- **symbols**: Key classes (ConfigDef, ConfigKey, AbstractConfig, PredicateDoc, TransformationDoc)
- **chain**: Dependency chain showing the pattern relationships
- **text**: Detailed narrative explanation of the configuration documentation pattern

Kafka\\n\\n### Pattern Overview\\nApache Kafka uses a class-based configuration pattern (not annotation-based) for defining and documenting configuration properties. While the task refers to @ConfigKey and @ConfigDef 'annotations', these do not exist as Java annotations in the Kafka codebase. Instead, Kafka uses:\\n\\n1. **ConfigDef class** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java): A class for specifying the set of expected configurations, with detailed metadata for each configuration key including name, type, default value, documentation, validator, importance level, group information, and dependency information.\\n\\n2. **ConfigKey inner class** (defined within ConfigDef.java, line 1237): A static inner class within ConfigDef that represents individual configuration keys with comprehensive metadata.\\n\\n3. **AbstractConfig class** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java): Base class extended by configuration classes throughout Kafka that holds parsed and original configuration values.\\n\\n### Configuration Documentation Generators\\nKafka provides documentation generation tools that extract configuration information at runtime:\\n\\n- **PredicateDoc** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/tools/PredicateDoc.java): Generates HTML documentation for Kafka Connect predicates by reflecting on OVERVIEW_DOC and CONFIG_DEF static fields.\\n\\n- **TransformationDoc** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/tools/TransformationDoc.java): Generates HTML documentation for Kafka Connect transformations (Cast, DropHeaders, ExtractField, Filter, Flatten, HeaderFrom, HoistField, InsertField, InsertHeader, MaskField, RegexRouter, ReplaceField, SetSchemaMetadata, TimestampConverter, TimestampRouter, ValueToKey).\\n\\n### AbstractConfig Subclasses\\nThroughout the Kafka codebase, 53+ classes extend AbstractConfig and define CONFIG_DEF static fields for configuration management. Key categories include:\\n\\n**Client-side configurations:**\\n- AdminClientConfig, ConsumerConfig, ProducerConfig\\n\\n**Kafka Connect configurations:**\\n- ConverterConfig, SimpleHeaderConverter, MirrorClientConfig, ConnectorConfig, SinkConnectorConfig, TaskConfig, WorkerConfig, RestServerConfig\\n- Converter implementations: ByteArrayConverter, BooleanConverter, NumberConverter\\n- Transform implementations: Cast, DropHeaders, ExtractField, Filter, Flatten, HeaderFrom, HoistField, InsertField, InsertHeader, MaskField, RegexRouter, ReplaceField, SetSchemaMetadata, TimestampConverter, TimestampRouter, ValueToKey\\n- Predicate implementations: HasHeaderKey, RecordIsTombstone, TopicNameMatches\\n\\n**Server-side configurations:**\\n- AbstractKafkaConfig, ServerConfigs, QuotaConfig, SocketServerConfigs, DelegationTokenManagerConfigs, KRaftConfigs, ReplicationConfigs, ClientMetricsConfigs, MetricConfigs, BrokerSecurityConfigs\\n\\n**Component-specific configurations:**\\n- GroupCoordinatorConfig, ShareGroupConfig, ShareCoordinatorConfig (coordinators)\\n- MetadataLogConfig, QuorumConfig (raft)\\n- LogConfig, CleanerConfig (storage)\\n- AddPartitionsToTxnConfig, TransactionLogConfig, TransactionStateManagerConfig (transaction coordinator)\\n- StreamsConfig, TopologyConfig (streams)\\n\\nThis pattern provides a declarative, strongly-typed approach to configuration management without requiring Java annotations, using reflection and static field discovery for documentation generation.\"\n}\n",

Kafka\\n\\n### Pattern Overview\\nApache Kafka uses a class-based configuration pattern (not annotation-based) for defining and documenting configuration properties. While the task refers to @ConfigKey and @ConfigDef 'annotations', these do not exist as Java annotations in the Kafka codebase. Instead, Kafka uses:\\n\\n1. **ConfigDef class** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java): A class for specifying the set of expected configurations, with detailed metadata for each configuration key including name, type, default value, documentation, validator, importance level, group information, and dependency information.\\n\\n2. **ConfigKey inner class** (defined within ConfigDef.java, line 1237): A static inner class within ConfigDef that represents individual configuration keys with comprehensive metadata.\\n\\n3. **AbstractConfig class** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java): Base class extended by configuration classes throughout Kafka that holds parsed and original configuration values.\\n\\n### Configuration Documentation Generators\\nKafka provides documentation generation tools that extract configuration information at runtime:\\n\\n- **PredicateDoc** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/tools/PredicateDoc.java): Generates HTML documentation for Kafka Connect predicates by reflecting on OVERVIEW_DOC and CONFIG_DEF static fields.\\n\\n- **TransformationDoc** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/tools/TransformationDoc.java): Generates HTML documentation for Kafka Connect transformations (Cast, DropHeaders, ExtractField, Filter, Flatten, HeaderFrom, HoistField, InsertField, InsertHeader, MaskField, RegexRouter, ReplaceField, SetSchemaMetadata, TimestampConverter, TimestampRouter, ValueToKey).\\n\\n### AbstractConfig Subclasses\\nThroughout the Kafka codebase, 53+ classes extend AbstractConfig and define CONFIG_DEF static fields for configuration management. Key categories include:\\n\\n**Client-side configurations:**\\n- AdminClientConfig, ConsumerConfig, ProducerConfig\\n\\n**Kafka Connect configurations:**\\n- ConverterConfig, SimpleHeaderConverter, MirrorClientConfig, ConnectorConfig, SinkConnectorConfig, TaskConfig, WorkerConfig, RestServerConfig\\n- Converter implementations: ByteArrayConverter, BooleanConverter, NumberConverter\\n- Transform implementations: Cast, DropHeaders, ExtractField, Filter, Flatten, HeaderFrom, HoistField, InsertField, InsertHeader, MaskField, RegexRouter, ReplaceField, SetSchemaMetadata, TimestampConverter, TimestampRouter, ValueToKey\\n- Predicate implementations: HasHeaderKey, RecordIsTombstone, TopicNameMatches\\n\\n**Server-side configurations:**\\n- AbstractKafkaConfig, ServerConfigs, QuotaConfig, SocketServerConfigs, DelegationTokenManagerConfigs, KRaftConfigs, ReplicationConfigs, ClientMetricsConfigs, MetricConfigs, BrokerSecurityConfigs\\n\\n**Component-specific configurations:**\\n- GroupCoordinatorConfig, ShareGroupConfig, ShareCoordinatorConfig (coordinators)\\n- MetadataLogConfig, QuorumConfig (raft)\\n- LogConfig, CleanerConfig (storage)\\n- AddPartitionsToTxnConfig, TransactionLogConfig, TransactionStateManagerConfig (transaction coordinator)\\n- StreamsConfig, TopologyConfig (streams)\\n\\nThis pattern provides a declarative, strongly-typed approach to configuration management without requiring Java annotations, using reflection and static field discovery for documentation generation.\"\n}\n",
